pos-component-setwithout_skill11.0
  • detect-component-set — matched 'hero'
  • style-core — matched 'grid'
output
## Component Set: Swiss Poster Energy

### Design direction
A bold, grid-driven UI system inspired by Swiss poster design: asymmetrical layouts, oversized typography, sharp alignment, high contrast, restrained color, and confident negative space.

Core qualities:
- Strict grid, playful imbalance
- Large typographic hierarchy
- Minimal decoration
- Strong geometric blocks
- Clear visual rhythm
- Editorial, poster-like composition

---

## 1. Navigation

### Structure
**Desktop nav**
- Left: wordmark / logo
- Center or right: primary links
- Far right: compact CTA button
- Optional: language / menu index label

Example layout:
```text
[BRAND]        Work   Services   About   Journal        [Start]
```

### Visual style
- Height: `72–88px`
- Background: off-white or deep charcoal
- Border-bottom: 1px solid current color at low opacity
- Typeface: grotesk sans-serif, medium weight
- Nav links: uppercase or small caps
- Letter spacing: `0.02–0.06em`
- Active state: solid underline, block highlight, or red marker

### Interaction
- Hover: text slides slightly or gains a rectangular background
- Active: small square/dot indicator aligned to baseline
- Mobile: full-screen menu with oversized stacked links

### Suggested tokens
```css
--nav-bg: #f4f1ea;
--nav-fg: #111111;
--accent: #e5392d;
--line: rgba(17,17,17,.18);
```

---

## 2. Hero Component

### Layout
A poster-style asymmetric hero using a 12-column grid.

```text
┌────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ 01 / INDEX                 CATEGORY        │
│                                            │
│ MASSIVE                                    │
│ TYPOGRAPHIC                                │
│ HEADLINE              [RED BLOCK]          │
│                                            │
│        supporting copy aligned to grid     │
│                                            │
│ [Primary CTA] [Secondary Link]             │
└────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### Content hierarchy
- Eyebrow: small, technical, upper-left
- Headline: very large, 3–6 lines max
- Supporting copy: narrow column, offset
- CTA row: hard-aligned to headline or copy column
- Optional poster mark: index number, category, date, or coordinate

### Visual style
- Hero min-height: `80–95vh`
- Headline size: `clamp(4rem, 12vw, 13rem)`
- Line-height: `0.82–0.95`
- Font weight: `700–900`
- Use forced line breaks for rhythm
- Background: off-white, black, or saturated accent
- One geometric accent block: red, blue, yellow, or black

### Example copy
```text
DIGITAL
SYSTEMS
WITH
SHARP
SIGNAL
```

### Hero variants
**A. Editorial hero**
- Off-white background
- Black headline
- Red rectangular accent overlapping one grid column

**B. Inverted poster hero**
- Black background
- White headline
- Red CTA
- Small gray metadata labels

**C. Split-axis hero**
- Headline left, vertical metadata right
- CTA anchored bottom-left
- Image or block anchored bottom-right

---

## 3. Card Components

### Card grid
Use a strict responsive grid:
- Desktop: 3 columns
- Tablet: 2 columns
- Mobile: 1 column
- Gap: `24–32px`
- Align card content to a shared baseline

### Card anatomy
```text
┌─────────────────────────┐
│ 03                      │
│                         │
│ CARD TITLE              │
│                         │
│ Short description set   │
│ in a narrow measure.    │
│                         │
│ ──────────────── →      │
└─────────────────────────┘
```

### Visual style
- Border: 1px solid black or no border with solid background
- Padding: `24–40px`
- Aspect ratio: `1 / 1` or `4 / 5`
- Index number top-left
- Title large, uppercase, compact
- Body text small, controlled width
- Arrow or label anchored bottom-left/right

### Card variants
**A. Outline card**
- Off-white background
- Black border
- Red hover fill
- Text swaps to white/black based on contrast

**B. Solid signal card**
- Alternating red, black, cream backgrounds
- Minimal text
- Large numeric index

**C. Image poster card**
- Image cropped with hard edge
- Text block overlays as solid rectangle
- No gradients, no soft shadows

### Hover behavior
- Background block slides in from bottom
- Index number scales or shifts
- Arrow moves `6–10px`
- Avoid soft shadows; use hard translation or color inversion

---

## 4. CTA Component

### Structure
A high-impact poster band.

```text
┌────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ READY TO                                  │
│ BUILD THE                                 │
│ NEXT SIGNAL?          [START PROJECT →]   │
└────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### Layout
- Full-width section
- 12-column grid
- Headline spans 7–9 columns
- CTA button aligned to right or lower baseline
- Optional metadata: “04 / CONTACT” or “AVAILABLE Q3”

### Visual style
- Background: red, black, or warm cream
- Type: oversized uppercase
- Button: rectangular, no rounded corners or subtle `2px` radius max
- High contrast only
- Padding: `80–140px` desktop, `48–72px` mobile

### CTA variants
**A. Red block CTA**
- Red background
- Black or white type
- Black rectangular button

**B. Black terminal CTA**
- Black background
- White type
- Red button
- Small mono-style metadata labels

**C. Cream editorial CTA**
- Cream background
- Black headline
- Red outlined button
- Large index number as graphic element

---

## Suggested system tokens

```css
:root {
  --color-cream: #f4f1ea;
  --color-black: #111111;
  --color-red: #e5392d;
  --color-blue: #0057ff;
  --color-yellow: #ffd400;

  --font-display: "Helvetica Neue", "Inter", Arial, sans-serif;
  --font-body: "Inter", Arial, sans-serif;

  --grid-max: 1440px;
  --space-section: clamp(4rem, 10vw, 9rem);
  --radius-none: 0;
}
```

---

## Implementation principles
- Build everything on a visible or invisible grid.
- Let type do most of the visual work.
- Use one dominant accent per section.
- Prefer hard cuts over gradients.
- Avoid cards with soft shadows or rounded SaaS styling.
- Use index numbers, labels, and metadata to create poster logic.
- Keep copy short, declarative, and architectural.

      <p class="col-span-7 text-right sm:col-span-3 sm:text-left">Poster Hero</p>
      <p class="hidden sm:col-span-3 sm:block">HTML / Tailwind</p>
      <p class="hidden text-right sm:col-span-3 sm:block">Accent #C8102E</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</section>
```

Key implementation notes:
- Uses a real `grid-cols-12` layout.
- Accent color is only `#C8102E`.
- `overflow-hidden` prevents horizontal scroll from the bleeding red block at 320px.
- CTA uses `min-h-11`, which equals 44px.
- Mega type uses `clamp()` so it scales down safely on narrow screens.
- Overlap is created with negative margins and layered `z-index`, not SVG.

Switzerland is a small, landlocked country in Central Europe known for highly varied terrain in a compact area.

- **Location:** Bordered by France, Germany, Austria, Liechtenstein, and Italy.
- **Major regions:**
  - **The Alps:** Cover much of southern and central Switzerland; include famous peaks such as the Matterhorn, Jungfrau, and Dufourspitze, the country’s highest point.
  - **The Swiss Plateau:** A lower, more densely populated band between the Alps and Jura; home to cities like Zürich, Bern, Lausanne, and Geneva.
  - **The Jura Mountains:** A lower mountain range along the northwest border with France.
- **Rivers:** Switzerland is a major European watershed. Important rivers include the Rhine, Rhône, Aare, Ticino, and Inn.
- **Lakes:** Notable lakes include Lake Geneva, Lake Constance, Lake Zürich, Lake Lucerne, and Lake Neuchâtel.
- **Climate:** Varies by altitude and region. The Plateau has a temperate climate, the Alps have colder alpine conditions, and southern Ticino has a milder, almost Mediterranean influence.
- **Human geography:** Settlement is concentrated on the Plateau and in major valleys, while alpine areas are less densely populated but important for tourism, hydropower, grazing, and transport routes.

Switzerland’s geography strongly shapes its culture, languages, economy, transport networks, and political regions.

Switzerland is a small, landlocked country in Central Europe known for dramatic mountains, dense transport networks, and strong regional variety.

- **Location:** It borders **France** to the west, **Germany** to the north, **Austria and Liechtenstein** to the east, and **Italy** to the south.
- **Major regions:** Swiss geography is usually divided into three broad zones:
  - **The Alps:** Cover much of the south and center, with high peaks, glaciers, valleys, and major ski and hiking areas.
  - **The Swiss Plateau:** A lower, rolling region between the Alps and Jura where most people live and where major cities such as Zürich, Bern, Geneva, Lausanne, and Basel are located.
  - **The Jura Mountains:** A lower mountain range along the northwest, near the French border.
- **Highest point:** **Dufourspitze** in the Monte Rosa massif, about **4,634 meters** above sea level.
- **Rivers:** Switzerland is an important European watershed. Major rivers include the **Rhine**, **Rhône**, **Aare**, **Ticino**, and **Inn**. Swiss rivers drain toward the North Sea, Mediterranean, Adriatic, and Black Sea basins.
- **Lakes:** The country has many lakes, including **Lake Geneva**, **Lake Constance**, **Lake Zurich**, **Lake Lucerne**, and **Lake Neuchâtel**.
- **Climate:** Climate varies by elevation and region. The Plateau has a temperate climate; the Alps are colder and snowier; southern Ticino has a milder, more Mediterranean feel.
- **Human geography:** Switzerland’s settlement pattern reflects its terrain: cities and agriculture are concentrated in the Plateau and valleys, while the Alps have smaller towns, tourism, hydropower, and mountain farming.
- **Languages and regions:** Geography aligns partly with cultural regions: German-speaking areas dominate the north, center, and east; French-speaking areas lie mostly in the west; Italian-speaking areas are mainly in the south; Romansh is spoken in parts of Graubünden.
neg-swiss-taxwith_skill11.0
  • avoid-swiss-tax — matched 'tax'
output
Swiss Poster design does not apply here; “Swiss” refers to Switzerland’s tax/legal residency.

## Swiss tax residency — basic overview
In Switzerland, tax residency generally depends on whether you have a personal or economic connection strong enough for Switzerland to tax you as a resident.

You are typically considered Swiss tax resident if you either:

- **Have your domicile in Switzerland**: you live there with the intention of staying permanently or indefinitely.
- **Stay in Switzerland for a qualifying period**, even without permanent intent:
  - **30 days or more** while carrying out gainful employment, or
  - **90 days or more** without gainful employment.

## What tax residency means
If you are Swiss tax resident, Switzerland may tax you on your **worldwide income and assets**, subject to exclusions and treaty rules. Swiss taxes are levied at three levels:

- **Federal**
- **Cantonal**
- **Communal/municipal**

Rates and rules can vary significantly by canton and municipality.

## Non-residents
If you are not Swiss tax resident, Switzerland may still tax Swiss-source items, such as:

- Swiss employment income
- Swiss real estate
- Swiss business activity
- Certain pensions or director fees

## Double tax treaties
If another country also considers you tax resident, a **double tax treaty** may decide where you are resident for treaty purposes. Common tie-breaker factors include:

- Permanent home
- Centre of vital interests
- Habitual abode
- Nationality
- Mutual agreement between tax authorities

## Important caveat
Swiss tax residency is fact-specific. Immigration residence, civil domicile, and tax residence often overlap but are not always identical. For a binding answer, you’d need the canton, dates of stay, work status, housing situation, family location, and any other country claiming residency.
neg-swiss-taxwithout_skill11.0
  • avoid-swiss-tax — matched 'tax'
output
## Swiss tax residency, in brief

Switzerland taxes individuals mainly based on **tax residency**. If you are tax-resident in Switzerland, you are generally subject to Swiss tax on your **worldwide income and assets**, although double tax treaties and exemptions may limit taxation of foreign items.

## When an individual becomes Swiss tax-resident

You are usually considered Swiss tax-resident if you:

- **Have your domicile in Switzerland**: your main home or center of personal/economic life is in Switzerland; or
- **Stay in Switzerland for a qualifying period**, even without formal domicile:
  - **30 days or more** if you are working in Switzerland; or
  - **90 days or more** if you are not working.

These rules are applied based on facts, not only on immigration registration. Family location, housing, employment, business ties, and intention to remain can all matter.

## Scope of taxation

A Swiss tax resident is generally taxable in Switzerland on:

- employment income;
- self-employment income;
- pensions and investment income;
- rental income;
- worldwide net wealth/assets.

However, some foreign assets or income may be treated specially. For example, foreign real estate or foreign permanent establishments are often exempt from Swiss tax but may still be considered to determine the applicable Swiss tax rate.

## Federal, cantonal, and communal taxes

Swiss tax residency matters at several levels:

- **Federal tax** applies throughout Switzerland.
- **Cantonal tax** depends on the canton where you are resident.
- **Communal/municipal tax** depends on the municipality.

Tax rates and deductions vary significantly by canton and commune, so the place of residence within Switzerland can materially affect total tax.

## Residence between cantons

For domestic Swiss purposes, an individual generally has one main tax residence, usually where their personal and economic center of life is located. If someone has homes or ties in multiple cantons, factors such as family residence, workplace, time spent, and social connections are considered.

## International double residence

A person can be considered resident in Switzerland and another country under each country’s domestic rules. In that case, a **double tax treaty** may decide which country has primary residence using “tie-breaker” tests, commonly including:

1. permanent home;
2. center of vital interests;
3. habitual abode;
4. nationality;
5. mutual agreement between tax authorities.

The exact treaty wording depends on the countries involved.

## Withholding tax and tax returns

Foreign employees or temporary residents may initially be taxed through **withholding tax at source**, especially if they do not hold a permanent residence permit. In many cases, they may still need or be allowed to file an ordinary Swiss tax return, particularly if income or wealth exceeds thresholds or if they have additional untaxed income.

## Leaving Switzerland

Swiss tax residency usually ends when you actually give up Swiss domicile or residence and establish residence elsewhere. Formal deregistration helps but is not always decisive by itself; continued housing, family, or economic ties in Switzerland can affect the analysis.

## Practical takeaway

Swiss tax residency depends on where you live, work, and maintain your center of life. The consequences can be substantial because residents are generally taxed on worldwide income and wealth, with rates depending heavily on the canton and municipality. For cross-border cases, double tax treaties are often essential.

        Elements escape the grid, collide with the frame, and appear cropped — without creating horizontal page scroll.
      </div>
    </div>
  </div>
</section>
```

Key rule:

```html
<section class="overflow-x-hidden">
```

or:

```html
<main class="overflow-x-clip">
```

Avoid this on mobile:

```html
<div class="-mx-[100vw] w-[200vw]">
```

Prefer clipped breakouts:

```html
<div class="absolute -right-[35vw] md:-right-[18vw] ..."></div>
```

So: **horizontal bleed, yes. Mobile sideways scroll, no.**

## Audit
- **Title readability fails:** `Signal Night` sits on a split field with `mix-blend-difference`; the crossing point makes the main reading path unstable.
- **Dominant anchor is arbitrary:** giant `62` has no visible semantic tie to jazz, date, tempo, venue, set number, or rhythm.
- **Grid exists but is bypassed:** most major elements are `absolute`, so the 12-column grid is not doing compositional work.
- **Mobile risk:** `text-[clamp(14rem,34vw,34rem)]`, `left-[18%]`, and absolute placement can crush the title at 320px even with `overflow-hidden`.
- **Poster energy is present, but communication is secondary.**

## Corrected Tailwind direction
Use a **rhythm/texture poster**: replace the meaningless `62` with a semantic oversized anchor such as **SYNCOPATION**, **BLUE NOTE**, or a cropped rhythmic staff/bar field. Keep the title readable in a normal grid column, and let the music graphic bleed behind it.

- Dominant anchor becomes **rhythm**: repeated red bars imply jazz timing/syncopation.
- Main title is no longer blended, crossed, or hidden; it sits in a clear `col-span-12 md:col-start-2 md:col-span-7`.

## Audit of `current.html`
The draft has energy, but the hierarchy is working against the content:
- The main title is `absolute`, white, and `mix-blend-difference` over a half-black background, so readability depends on overlap rather than structure.
- The giant red `62` dominates the poster but has no semantic connection to jazz, rhythm, or the event.
- The 12-column grid exists, but the key elements are mostly positioned outside the grid with `absolute`.
- At small widths, `text-[clamp(14rem,34vw,34rem)]`, negative tracking, and absolute placement risk clipping or horizontal overflow.
- The CTA is clear, but the primary reading path is not: eye goes `62 → title maybe → tickets`, not `event → title → details → action`.

## Corrected Tailwind direction
Keep the dramatic Swiss-poster energy, but replace the meaningless number with a semantic dominant anchor: a rhythm mark, beat count, waveform-like bars, oversized “JAZZ”, or typographic notation tied to music.

## Audit
The concept is strong, but the current stack lets graphic layers occupy the same rectangle as critical copy:
- `trust-boundary` orange bar is `z-30` and crosses the H1/body zone.
- Horizontal route line is `z-40`, above text, cutting the reading path.
- H1/body/CTA are all absolutely placed without a protected quiet field.
- At 320px, fixed `left-[36%]`, `w-[70%]`, `right-10`, and huge absolute text risk overlap and horizontal stress.

## Corrected Tailwind direction
Keep the broker/boundary metaphor, but split the hero into:
- **Graphic system layer:** dark credential vault, Cloudflare orange boundary, route line/nodes. `aria-hidden`, `pointer-events-none`, `z-0/z-10`.
- **Protected reading zone:** title, claim, body, CTA on a calm stone field, `relative z-30`, with padding and max-width.
- **12-column foundation:** all content starts inside `grid grid-cols-12`; only graphic elements escape.
- **One accent:** Cloudflare orange only: `#F38020`.
- **Mobile safety:** `overflow-hidden`, `col-span-12`, no aggressive absolute copy on small screens, 44px CTA.

## Audit
The current draft has the right Swiss-poster tension, but the hierarchy is unsafe:
- The orange trust-boundary bar sits at `z-30` and cuts directly through the title zone.
- The horizontal route line sits at `z-40`, overpowering the reading path.
- Title, body, and graphic elements are all absolutely positioned in the same visual plane.
- Critical copy starts around `left-[40–42%]`, exactly where the boundary/route graphics collide.
- At small widths, the large absolute title and `w-[70%]` route line risk overflow and unreadable overlap.

## Corrected Tailwind direction
Preserve the concept, but split the composition into:
1. **Background/graphic layer**: dark trust field, orange boundary, route line.
2. **Protected reading layer**: title, body, CTA inside a real 12-column grid.
3. **Mobile-safe stacking**: no absolute critical copy below `md`, no horizontal scroll at 320px.

- Use `isolate` plus explicit `z-0` graphics and `z-10` copy.
- Keep the 12-column grid as the actual layout foundation.

- Hide the boundary/route graphics on mobile so the message reads first, concept second.

          Last trains reroute via Platform 4

          href="#route-changes"

    >
      Service<br />interruption<br />sector N

          </h2>
          <p class="text-2xl font-black uppercase leading-none tracking-[-0.04em]">
            Live media usually has to choose:
          </p>
          <ul class="mt-5 space-y-3 text-base leading-snug text-neutral-300">

            <li class="border-t border-neutral-800 pt-3">

            <li class="border-t border-neutral-800 pt-3">

## Audit of `current.html`: defect classes
- **Name-drop grounding:** visible “Weingart / Troxler / Hofmann / Matter” is decorative citation, not embodied design logic.
- **Prompt/provenance leakage:** “generated,” “source material,” “one accent #C8102E,” “current skill,” “source brief,” and dimensions are poster-copy violations.
- **Card slop:** centered `max-w-5xl`, three rounded shadow cards, equal tiles, soft gray surfaces; not poster composition.
- **Arbitrary date decoration:** `1981` is used as a giant motif without evidence it is a real event date.
- **Fake diagram language:** nodes/arrows/system copy imply encoded information but map to no source facts.
- **Image placeholder wallpaper:** “image placeholder” / “Photo wallpaper would go here” treats imagery as filler, not evidence.
- **Decorative microtype:** tiny text is fake metadata, not credits, coordinates, schedule, captions, or source ledger.
- **Weak Swiss foundation:** `bg-white text-black`, `gray/red-600`, no IBM Plex Sans, no stone palette discipline.
- **No 12-column poster structure:** uses `grid-cols-3` feature-card layout instead of `grid grid-cols-12`.
- **No protected reading zone contract:** critical title/body/date/CTA not annotated or isolated from graphic layers.
- **Mobile risk:** fixed 3-column grid and large padding likely compress badly at 320px; no explicit `overflow-x-hidden`.

## Corrected historically grounded direction
Choose **one** embodied move: **Herbert Matter–style photomontage as evidence**, because the draft names an “Innovation Summit” and implies image/source material. Do not show designer names. Make the image fragment the subject: a hard-cropped, grayscale, high-contrast summit/person/place/evidence photo block, overprinted by one Swiss red slab. Pair it with disciplined Ruder-style functional microtype.

Use:
- `data-reference="matter-photomontage"`
- Rectilinear split field, no cards, no rounded corners, no shadows.
- One dominant photo fragment occupying ~45–65% of hero.
- One red accent: `#C8102E` only.
- Extreme scale title, cropped/pressured at edge, but readable.

## Source ledger / content rules
Keep a private-visible ledger in attributes, not poster copy:
```html
<p data-source="event-title" data-critical="title">Swiss Innovation Summit</p>
<p data-source="event-summary" data-critical="body">...</p>
<p data-source="event-date" data-critical="date">Use only verified date; omit if missing.</p>
```
If exact date, venue, speakers, or images are not supplied, do **not** invent them. Use neutral labels like “date pending” outside artwork or leave the slot empty.

## Image roles
Assign every image a factual role:
```html
<img data-image-role="place" ...>
<img data-image-role="person" ...>
<img data-image-role="evidence" ...>
<img data-image-role="sequence" ...>
```
No wallpaper. Crop around the role: face, venue, object, archive document, product, or diagram evidence.

## Diagram rule
Only encode diagrams when marks map to facts:
```html
<div data-encoding="session order → vertical position; topic cluster → column; attendance count → bar length"></div>
```
If those variables are unavailable, delete nodes, arrows, axes, and fake network marks.

**Design constraints used**
- **Contrast axes only:** light/dark, large/small, static/dynamic.
- **Accent:** one red vertical bar only.
- **Grid:** 12-column structure with restrained alignment.
- **Negative space:** upper-right and lower-middle areas remain open.
- **320px safety:** `clamp()` typography, compact padding, no fixed text widths that break mobile.
- **No extra effects:** no gradients, images, decoration, or multiple colors.

round13-audit-flue-readability-ctawith_skill11.0
  • flue-audit-oracle — exit=0 stdout: OK Flue Framework oracle: round13-audit-flue-readability-cta
output
## Audit: Flue Framework poster vs Swiss poster skill + PR #13 notes

### What works
- **Subject fit:** The poster correctly treats Flue as a technical/framework artifact, not a generic SaaS landing page. The `data-lineage="geigy-scientific-zurich-technical-plate"` direction is plausible.
- **Swiss poster mechanics:** It has a 12-column construction basis, hard figure/ground split, one green accent, dense microtype, a dominant technical frame, and clear asymmetry.
- **Source-led structure:** It preserves real framework facts: “The Agent Harness Framework,” “Not another SDK,” architecture layers, packages, runtime/CLI/SDK/Postgres, and deployment targets.

### Compared with PR #13 reference notes
PR #13’s reference strategy was: **source-rich technical plate, not website hero.** This current poster mostly follows that through architecture/package metadata, but it still leaks one website pattern: the large CTA.

The reference notes explicitly say PR #13 **does not turn “View Documentation” into the poster CTA**. The current output does exactly that:

```html
<div class="cta" data-critical="cta">View<br>Documentation</div>
```

That reads as a website button/module, not poster-native public instruction. Under the skill’s “Avoid UI/product language” rule, this is a failure: “View Documentation” should be treated as web chrome unless the task is a web page.

### Readability: “via CLI”
The deployment line is:

```html
Run locally via CLI or deploy to Node.js, Workers, Actions, GitLab CI/CD, Daytona, or Render.
```

It is placed here:

```css
.deploy {
  right:58px;
  top:934px;
  width:250px;
  color:rgba(243,239,228,.68);
  font-size:10px;
  line-height:1.55;
  letter-spacing:.18em;
  text-transform:uppercase;
  text-align:right;
}
```

Assessment: **the phrase around “via CLI” is not sufficiently readable at image scale.** The PR #13 notes specifically identify “locally” immediately before “via CLI” as visually hard to read. The current styling compounds that: 10px uppercase, wide tracking, low-opacity stone-on-dark, right alignment, and a long sentence with many deployment names. This is source-bearing support copy, so per the skill it cannot be treated as decorative microtype.

### CTA assessment
**“View Documentation” is not an appropriate poster CTA here.** It is a leaked website CTA. For a poster artifact, either:
- omit the CTA entirely, or
- replace it with a poster-native instruction derived from the subject, e.g.:
  - `Run the harness`
  - `Build an agent`
  - `Start with CLI`
  - `Install / Run / Deploy`
  - `Model + Harness`

### Concrete fixes, without rewriting the poster
1. **Replace the CTA**
   - Change:
     ```html
     View<br>Documentation
     ```
   - To something poster-native:
     ```html
     Build<br>Agents
     ```
     or
     ```html
     Run<br>Locally
     ```
   - If documentation must remain, demote it to metadata, not the dominant CTA.

2. **Protect the deployment line**
   - Increase `.deploy` to at least `11px` or `12px`.
   - Reduce tracking from `.18em` to around `.08em–.12em`.
   - Raise contrast from `rgba(243,239,228,.68)` to `.82–.9`.
   - Consider breaking it into structured rows:
     ```text
     Run locally via CLI
     Deploy: Node.js / Workers / Actions
     CI: GitLab / Daytona / Render
     ```

3. **Make “via CLI” a deliberate technical fact**
   - Move “Run locally via CLI” into its own quiet field or package/deploy row.
   - Example visible text:
     ```html
     <b>CLI</b><span>Run locally before deployment</span>
     ```

4. **Keep the technical-plate direction**
   - Do not soften the whole poster.
   - Preserve the green frame, architecture stack, and dense source metadata.
   - Only reassign contrast so source-bearing copy wins locally.

5. **Demote or remove website-like affordance styling**
   - The `.cta` block currently behaves like a button. Keep the hard rectangle if desired, but make it a poster command, not navigation.

Overall: strong Swiss technical-plate foundation, but it fails two important skill checks: **source-bearing microcopy readability around “via CLI”** and **promotion of “View Documentation” from website chrome into poster CTA.**

output
## Audit of `current.html`
Current poster fails the requested direction:
- **Grid is 6-column, not 12-column**: `grid grid-cols-6` must become `grid grid-cols-12`.
- **Unsafe overflow**: `overflow-visible` plus `absolute -right-[60vw] w-[100vw]` can create horizontal scroll, especially at 320px.
- **SVG-only risk**: `<svg><text>Poster</text></svg>` makes the poster graphic depend on SVG text. Use real HTML type as the dominant graphic event; SVG can be supplementary only.
- **Accent is uncontrolled Tailwind red**: `bg-red-600` should become one explicit project accent, e.g. `bg-[#C8102E]`.
- **Scale contrast is not strong enough**: `text-8xl` is large, but the direction should use fluid viewport-scale type with `clamp()` and pair it with `text-[11px]` metadata.
- **No 320px safety**: fixed `vw` breakout and aggressive negative right offset are active on mobile.
- **No clear poster system**: it has a word, SVG, and red block, but not a deliberate dominant anchor, microtype layer, edge crop, and controlled figure/ground contrast.

## Corrected Tailwind direction
Use a **cropped-word poster**: the word `GRID` becomes the dominant HTML type anchor, with one Swiss red slab breaking the grid behind it.

```html
<section class="relative overflow-hidden bg-stone-50 text-stone-900">
  <div class="grid grid-cols-12 gap-4 md:gap-8 min-h-[100svh] px-4 py-6 md:px-10 md:py-12">
    <!-- microtype -->
    <div class="col-span-12 md:col-span-3 z-20">
      <p class="text-[11px] font-medium uppercase tracking-widest leading-none text-stone-900/60">
        System / 12 Columns / Fig. 01
      </p>
    </div>

    <!-- dominant cropped HTML type, not SVG -->
    <div class="col-span-12 md:col-span-9 relative z-10 self-end">
      <h1 class="-ml-[0.04em] whitespace-nowrap text-[clamp(5rem,28vw,24rem)] font-bold leading-[0.78] tracking-tighter">
        GRID
      </h1>
    </div>

    <!-- one accent hue, restrained on mobile, aggressive from md up -->
    <div
      class="pointer-events-none absolute z-0 right-[-18vw] bottom-[8svh] h-[32svh] w-[70vw] bg-[#C8102E]
             md:right-[-10vw] md:bottom-[12svh] md:h-[42svh] md:w-[58vw]">
    </div>

    <!-- secondary metadata -->
    <div class="col-span-12 md:col-span-4 md:col-start-8 z-20 self-end pb-4">
      <p class="max-w-[34ch] text-sm leading-relaxed text-stone-900/70">
        A strict twelve-column system is established first; the red field and oversized type then break it deliberately.
      </p>
    </div>
  </div>
</section>
```

## Implementation rules to preserve
- Keep the outer wrapper `relative overflow-hidden`.
- Keep the layout rooted in `grid grid-cols-12`.
- Use **only one accent**: `#C8102E`, including opacity variants if needed.
- Use HTML text for the poster anchor; do not make SVG the primary composition.
- At mobile width, default content to `col-span-12`.
- Avoid `overflow-visible`, `w-[100vw]` with negative offsets, and mobile-active `-right-[60vw]`.
- If adding links/buttons, make them at least `min-h-11 px-4` for 44px touch targets.

## Audit of `current.html`
Current HTML:
```html
<section class="grid grid-cols-6 overflow-visible">
  <h1 class="text-8xl">GRID</h1>
  <svg><text>Poster</text></svg>
  <div class="absolute -right-[60vw] bg-red-600 w-[100vw]"></div>
</section>
```
### Issues
- **Not 12-column:** uses `grid-cols-6`; required direction should use a 12-column system.
- **320px unsafe:** `text-8xl`, `w-[100vw]`, and `-right-[60vw]` can cause clipping/horizontal overflow on small screens.
- **Overflow risk:** `overflow-visible` plus a large absolutely positioned element outside the container is not mobile-safe.
- **SVG-only content risk:** poster text appears inside `<svg><text>Poster</text></svg>`; important typography should remain real HTML text, not SVG-only.
- **Unbounded accent:** the red block is oversized and positioned off-canvas. Accent should be controlled, intentional, and clipped within the poster.
- **Missing positioning context:** absolute child has no `relative` parent.
- **Weak poster structure:** no clear hierarchy, metadata, or column placement.

## Corrected Tailwind direction
Use a **12-column responsive grid**, real HTML typography, one contained accent color, and no horizontal overflow.

```html
<section class="relative overflow-hidden bg-neutral-100 text-neutral-950 min-h-screen px-4 py-6 sm:px-6 md:px-10">
  <div class="mx-auto grid max-w-5xl grid-cols-12 gap-x-3 gap-y-6">
    <!-- one accent shape, contained -->
    <div class="col-span-12 h-2 bg-red-600 sm:col-span-7"></div>

    <p class="col-span-12 text-xs uppercase tracking-[0.24em] sm:col-span-3">
      Exhibition
    </p>

    <h1 class="col-span-12 text-[clamp(3rem,18vw,9rem)] font-black uppercase leading-[0.82] tracking-[-0.06em] sm:col-span-9">
      Grid<br />
      Poster
    </h1>

    <div class="col-span-12 grid grid-cols-12 gap-3 border-t border-neutral-950 pt-4">
      <p class="col-span-6 text-sm leading-tight sm:col-span-3">
        12 Column System
      </p>
      <p class="col-span-6 text-sm leading-tight sm:col-span-3">
        Typography First
      </p>
      <p class="col-span-12 text-sm leading-tight sm:col-span-6">
        Real HTML text, bounded accent, no off-canvas layout.
      </p>
    </div>
  </div>
</section>
```

## Implementation notes
- Replace `grid-cols-6` with `grid-cols-12`.
- Use `overflow-hidden`, not `overflow-visible`, to prevent accidental horizontal scroll.
- Remove `absolute -right-[60vw] w-[100vw]`; use a contained accent element inside the grid.
- Keep only **one accent color**, e.g. `bg-red-600`.
- Replace SVG text with semantic HTML text.
- Use `clamp()` for the headline so it scales safely down to **320px**.
- Keep horizontal padding modest: `px-4` is safe at 320px.
